Conversely, assume that π𝜋\pi is (t^,η^)^𝑡^𝜂(\hat{t},\hat{\eta})-valid. Consider i∈[n]𝑖delimited-[]𝑛i\in[n]. Recall that Si={z^i}subscript𝑆𝑖subscript^𝑧𝑖S_{i}=\left\{{\hat{z}_{i}}\right\} and fi​(z^i)=0subscript𝑓𝑖subscript^𝑧𝑖0f_{i}(\hat{z}_{i})=0. By condition (VA.1), we have z^i∈π​(i)subscript^𝑧𝑖𝜋𝑖\hat{z}_{i}\in\pi(i). By the definition of a (t^,η^)^𝑡^𝜂(\hat{t},\hat{\eta})-valid allocation, π𝜋\pi has a (t,η,i)𝑡𝜂𝑖(t,\eta,i)-witness, say Hi′subscriptsuperscript𝐻′𝑖H^{\prime}_{i}. By condition (VA.2)(VA.2)(c), for every z∈π​(i)∖{z^i}𝑧𝜋𝑖subscript^𝑧𝑖z\in\pi(i)\setminus\left\{{\hat{z}_{i}}\right\}, we have distHi′​(z^i,z)≤βsubscriptdistsubscriptsuperscript𝐻′𝑖subscript^𝑧𝑖𝑧𝛽\text{dist}_{H^{\prime}_{i}}(\hat{z}_{i},z)\leq\beta, which implies that distG​[π​(i)]​(z^i,z)≤βsubscriptdist𝐺delimited-[]𝜋𝑖subscript^𝑧𝑖𝑧𝛽\text{dist}_{G[\pi(i)]}(\hat{z}_{i},z)\leq\beta. Thus ((z^i)i∈[n];β)subscriptsubscript^𝑧𝑖𝑖delimited-[]𝑛𝛽((\hat{z}_{i})_{i\in[n]};\beta)-annotated.∎

Lemma 6.7 tells us that to check if (G,N,𝒱)𝐺𝑁𝒱(G,N,\mathcal{V}) admits a ((z^i)i∈[n];β)subscriptsubscript^𝑧𝑖𝑖delimited-[]𝑛𝛽((\hat{z}_{i})_{i\in[n]};\beta)-annotated allocation, it is sufficient to check if (G,N,𝒱)𝐺𝑁𝒱(G,N,\mathcal{V}) admits a (t^,η^)^𝑡^𝜂(\hat{t},\hat{\eta})-valid allocation. In light of this, we now define the states of our DP as follows. For each t∈V​(T)𝑡𝑉𝑇\bm{t\in V(T)} and each tuple η∈𝒞t𝜂subscript𝒞𝑡\bm{\eta\in\mathcal{C}_{t}}, we defineA​[t,η]=𝟏𝐴𝑡𝜂1\bm{A[t,\eta]=1} if there exists a (t,η)𝑡𝜂\bm{(t,\eta)}-valid allocation and A​[t,η]=𝟎𝐴𝑡𝜂0\bm{A[t,\eta]=0} otherwise.

Assuming the correctness of Lemma 6.3 and assuming that we can correctly compute A​[t,η]𝐴𝑡𝜂A[t,\eta] for every t∈V​(T)𝑡𝑉𝑇t\in V(T) and η∈𝒞t𝜂subscript𝒞𝑡\eta\in\mathcal{C}_{t}, let us now complete the proof of Theorem 6.1.

We show how we can use Lemma 6.3 as well as the definition of A​[t,η]𝐴𝑡𝜂A[t,\eta] to solve [𝚇]delimited-[]𝚇[\mathtt{X}]-Annotated-FD. Consider an instance (G,[n],𝒱,(z^i)i∈[n],β)𝐺delimited-[]𝑛𝒱subscriptsubscript^𝑧𝑖𝑖delimited-[]𝑛𝛽(G,[n],\mathcal{V},(\hat{z}_{i})_{i\in[n]},\beta) of [𝚇]delimited-[]𝚇[\mathtt{X}]-Annotated-FD.

First, proportionality. For i∈[n]𝑖delimited-[]𝑛i\in[n], let Wi=vi​(V​(G))subscript𝑊𝑖subscript𝑣𝑖𝑉𝐺W_{i}=v_{i}(V(G)). Otherwise, we return no.

Now, envy-freeness. We go over all possible tuples (wi​j)i,j∈[n]subscriptsubscript𝑤𝑖𝑗𝑖𝑗delimited-[]𝑛(w_{ij})_{i,j\in[n]} where for every i∈[n]𝑖delimited-[]𝑛i\in[n], w^i​i≥w^i​jsubscript^𝑤𝑖𝑖subscript^𝑤𝑖𝑗\hat{w}_{ii}\geq\hat{w}_{ij} for every j∈[n]∖{i}𝑗delimited-[]𝑛𝑖j\in[n]\setminus\left\{{i}\right\}. For each such tuple (wi​j)i,j∈[n]subscriptsubscript𝑤𝑖𝑗𝑖𝑗delimited-[]𝑛(w_{ij})_{i,j\in[n]}, we invoke the algorithm of Lemma 6.3 and return yes or no accordingly.

Notice that for both proportionality and envy-freeness, the number of tuples (w^i​j)i,j∈[n]subscriptsubscript^𝑤𝑖𝑗𝑖𝑗delimited-[]𝑛(\hat{w}_{ij})_{i,j\in[n]} that we considered is always upper bounded by W𝒪​(n2)superscript𝑊𝒪superscript𝑛2W^{\mathcal{O}(n^{2})}.

To solve the maximin fair variant of the problem, let us first see how we can compute the maximin share guarantee for each agent. We can use a similar approach to decide if there is a welfare-maximising ((z^i)i∈[n];β)subscriptsubscript^𝑧𝑖𝑖delimited-[]𝑛𝛽((\hat{z}_{i})_{i\in[n]};\beta)-annotated allocation as well. We now show how to compute A​[t,η]𝐴𝑡𝜂A[t,\eta] recursively. For each t∈V​(T)𝑡𝑉𝑇t\in V(T), we compute A​[t,η]𝐴𝑡𝜂A[t,\eta], assuming that we have computed A​[t′,η′]𝐴superscript𝑡′superscript𝜂′A[t^{\prime},\eta^{\prime}] correctly for all descendants t′superscript𝑡′t^{\prime} of t𝑡t and all η′∈𝒞t′superscript𝜂′subscript𝒞superscript𝑡′\eta^{\prime}\in\mathcal{C}_{t^{\prime}}. In all the cases below, η=((Si,fi,(𝒫i,Ri))i∈[n],(wi​j)i,j∈[n])𝜂subscriptsubscript𝑆𝑖subscript𝑓𝑖subscript𝒫𝑖subscript𝑅𝑖𝑖delimited-[]𝑛subscriptsubscript𝑤𝑖𝑗𝑖𝑗delimited-[]𝑛\eta=((S_{i},f_{i},(\mathcal{P}_{i},R_{i}))_{i\in[n]},(w_{ij})_{i,j\in[n]}).

Let t𝑡t be a forget node and t′superscript𝑡′t^{\prime} the unique child of t𝑡t.Let Xt=Xt′∖{z}subscript𝑋𝑡subscript𝑋superscript𝑡′𝑧X_{t}=X_{t^{\prime}}\setminus\left\{{z}\right\} for some z∈Xt′𝑧subscript𝑋superscript𝑡′z\in X_{t^{\prime}}.Then z∉{z^1,z^2,…,z^n}𝑧subscript^𝑧1subscript^𝑧2…subscript^𝑧𝑛z\notin\left\{{\hat{z}_{1},\hat{z}_{2},\ldots,\hat{z}_{n}}\right\} and Gt=Gt′subscript𝐺𝑡subscript𝐺superscript𝑡′G_{t}=G_{t^{\prime}}.

Suppose that we have a (t,η)𝑡𝜂(t,\eta)-valid allocation, say π𝜋\pi.Notice that π𝜋\pi may or may not allocate the vertex z𝑧z.If π𝜋\pi does not allocate z𝑧z, then π𝜋\pi is (t′,η)superscript𝑡′𝜂(t^{\prime},\eta)-valid as well (and we can simply ignore z𝑧z).On the other hand, if π𝜋\pi does allocate z𝑧z to agent i𝑖i for some i∈[n]𝑖delimited-[]𝑛i\in[n], then notice that π​(i)∩Xt′=Si∪{z}𝜋𝑖subscript𝑋superscript𝑡′subscript𝑆𝑖𝑧\pi(i)\cap X_{t^{\prime}}=S_{i}\cup\left\{{z}\right\}, and z𝑧z must be present in one of the blocks of 𝒫i′subscriptsuperscript𝒫′𝑖\mathcal{P}^{\prime}_{i}, where 𝒫i′subscriptsuperscript𝒫′𝑖\mathcal{P}^{\prime}_{i} is a partition obtained from 𝒫isubscript𝒫𝑖\mathcal{P}_{i} by adding z𝑧z to one of the blocks of 𝒫isubscript𝒫𝑖\mathcal{P}_{i}.We formalise this intuition as follows.

Forget)

Notice that while combining π′superscript𝜋′\pi^{\prime} and π′′superscript𝜋′′\pi^{\prime\prime} to form π𝜋\pi , we must also ensure that we count agent i𝑖i’s valuation for π​(j)∩Xt=Sj𝜋𝑗subscript𝑋𝑡subscript𝑆𝑗\pi(j)\cap X_{t}=S_{j} (i.e., vi​(Sj)subscript𝑣𝑖subscript𝑆𝑗v_{i}(S_{j})) only once. We formalise this intuition as follows.

We relegate the formal proof of correctness of our computation to the appendix (see Lemma 6.8). To complete the proof of Lemma 6.3, let us analyse the runtime of our DP. By Observation 6.4, we have |𝒞t|≤(𝗍𝗐+n)𝒪​(𝗍𝗐+n)⋅β𝒪​(𝗍𝗐)⋅W𝒪​(n2)subscript𝒞𝑡⋅superscript𝗍𝗐𝑛𝒪𝗍𝗐𝑛superscript𝛽𝒪𝗍𝗐superscript𝑊𝒪superscript𝑛2{|{\mathcal{C}_{t}}|}\leq({\sf tw}+n)^{\mathcal{O}({\sf tw}+n)}\cdot\beta^{\mathcal{O}({\sf tw})}\cdot W^{\mathcal{O}(n^{2})}. And since we work with a nice tree decomposition, |V​(T)|=m𝒪​(1)𝑉𝑇superscript𝑚𝒪1{|{V(T)}|}=m^{\mathcal{O}(1)}. Hence the number of states of the DP is at most (𝗍𝗐+n)𝒪​(𝗍𝗐+n)⋅β𝒪​(𝗍𝗐)⋅W𝒪​(n2)⋅m𝒪​(1)⋅superscript𝗍𝗐𝑛𝒪𝗍𝗐𝑛superscript𝛽𝒪𝗍𝗐superscript𝑊𝒪superscript𝑛2superscript𝑚𝒪1({\sf tw}+n)^{\mathcal{O}({\sf tw}+n)}\cdot\beta^{\mathcal{O}({\sf tw})}\cdot W^{\mathcal{O}(n^{2})}\cdot m^{\mathcal{O}(1)}. Hence the runtime follows. This completes the proof of Lemma 6.3.

Consider t∈V​(T)𝑡𝑉𝑇t\in V(T) and η∈𝒞t𝜂subscript𝒞𝑡\eta\in\mathcal{C}_{t}. Let η=(((Si,fi,(𝒫i,Ri))i∈[n],wi​j)i,j∈[n])𝜂subscriptsubscriptsubscript𝑆𝑖subscript𝑓𝑖subscript𝒫𝑖subscript𝑅𝑖𝑖delimited-[]𝑛subscript𝑤𝑖𝑗𝑖𝑗delimited-[]𝑛\eta=(((S_{i},f_{i},(\mathcal{P}_{i},R_{i}))_{i\in[n]},w_{ij})_{i,j\in[n]}).

We prove the lemma by induction on t𝑡t. That is, assuming that A​[t′,η′]𝐴superscript𝑡′superscript𝜂′A[t^{\prime},\eta^{\prime}] is computed correctly for all descendants t′superscript𝑡′t^{\prime} of t𝑡t and η′∈𝒞t′superscript𝜂′superscriptsubscript𝒞𝑡′\eta^{\prime}\in\mathcal{C}_{t}^{\prime}, we prove that A​[t,η]𝐴𝑡𝜂A[t,\eta] is computed correctly as well. The base case of the induction is when t𝑡t is a leaf node.

Suppose that t𝑡t is a leaf node. Then Xt={z^1,z^2,…,z^n}subscript𝑋𝑡subscript^𝑧1subscript^𝑧2…subscript^𝑧𝑛X_{t}=\left\{{\hat{z}_{1},\hat{z}_{2},\ldots,\hat{z}_{n}}\right\} and Gtsubscript𝐺𝑡G_{t} is the edgeless graph containing the n𝑛n vertices z^1,z^2,…,z^nsubscript^𝑧1subscript^𝑧2…subscript^𝑧𝑛\hat{z}_{1},\hat{z}_{2},\ldots,\hat{z}_{n}. Assume that A​[t,η]=1𝐴𝑡𝜂1A[t,\eta]=1. There are two possible cases: either π𝜋\pi does not allocate z𝑧z or π𝜋\pi does allocate z𝑧z.

Suppose that π𝜋\pi does not allocate z𝑧z. That is, z∉⋃i=1nπ​(i)𝑧superscriptsubscript𝑖1𝑛𝜋𝑖z\notin\bigcup_{i=1}^{n}\pi(i). Then, since z∈Xt𝑧subscript𝑋𝑡z\in X_{t} and since π𝜋\pi is (t,η)𝑡𝜂(t,\eta)-valid, we have z∉⋃i=1nSi𝑧superscriptsubscript𝑖1𝑛subscript𝑆𝑖z\notin\bigcup_{i=1}^{n}S_{i}. In this case, 6 sets A​[t,η]𝐴𝑡𝜂A[t,\eta] to be A​[t′,η]𝐴superscript𝑡′𝜂A[t^{\prime},\eta]. First, since z∉⋃i=1nSi𝑧superscriptsubscript𝑖1𝑛subscript𝑆𝑖z\notin\bigcup_{i=1}^{n}S_{i}, we have S1,S2,…,Sn⊆Xt′subscript𝑆1subscript𝑆2…subscript𝑆𝑛subscript𝑋superscript𝑡′S_{1},S_{2},\ldots,S_{n}\subseteq X_{t^{\prime}} and hence η∈Ct′𝜂subscript𝐶superscript𝑡′\eta\in C_{t^{\prime}}. Since z∉⋃i=1nπ​(i)𝑧superscriptsubscript𝑖1𝑛𝜋𝑖z\notin\bigcup_{i=1}^{n}\pi(i), and since the graphs Gtsubscript𝐺𝑡G_{t} and Gt′subscript𝐺superscript𝑡′G_{t^{\prime}} differ only in the isolated vertex z𝑧z, observe that π𝜋\pi is (t′,η)superscript𝑡′𝜂(t^{\prime},\eta)-valid as well. Hence A​[t′,η]=1𝐴superscript𝑡′𝜂1A[t^{\prime},\eta]=1. By the induction hypothesis, A​[t′,η]𝐴superscript𝑡′𝜂A[t^{\prime},\eta] is computed correctly, and we can thus conclude that 6 correctly assigns the value 111 to A​[t,η]𝐴𝑡𝜂A[t,\eta] in this case.

The case when H′superscript𝐻′H^{\prime} is a connected component of Hi′′subscriptsuperscript𝐻′′𝑖H^{\prime\prime}_{i} is identical.∎

We have thus shown that 𝒫isubscript𝒫𝑖\mathcal{P}_{i} is indeed the partition of Sisubscript𝑆𝑖S_{i} into the connected components of 𝙶​(𝒫i′,𝒫i′′)𝙶subscriptsuperscript𝒫′𝑖subscriptsuperscript𝒫′′𝑖\mathtt{G}(\mathcal{P}^{\prime}_{i},\mathcal{P}^{\prime\prime}_{i}). To complete the proof, we only need to prove that 𝙶​(𝒫i′,𝒫i′′)𝙶subscriptsuperscript𝒫′𝑖subscriptsuperscript𝒫′′𝑖\mathtt{G}(\mathcal{P}^{\prime}_{i},\mathcal{P}^{\prime\prime}_{i}) is acyclic. But observe that for every edge x​y∈E​(𝙶​(𝒫i′))𝑥𝑦𝐸𝙶subscriptsuperscript𝒫′𝑖xy\in E(\mathtt{G}(\mathcal{P}^{\prime}_{i})), there exists a corresponding x𝑥x-y𝑦y path in Hi′subscriptsuperscript𝐻′𝑖H^{\prime}_{i}, which is an x𝑥x-y𝑦y path in Hisubscript𝐻𝑖H_{i}. And for every edge x​y∈𝙶​(𝒫i′′)𝑥𝑦𝙶subscriptsuperscript𝒫′′𝑖xy\in\mathtt{G}(\mathcal{P}^{\prime\prime}_{i}), there exists a corresponding x𝑥x-y𝑦y path in Hi′′subscriptsuperscript𝐻′′𝑖H^{\prime\prime}_{i}, which is also a path in Hisubscript𝐻𝑖H_{i}.Recall now that E​(𝙶​(𝒫i′,𝒫i′′))=E​(𝙶​(𝒫i′))∪E​(𝙶​(𝒫i′))𝐸𝙶subscriptsuperscript𝒫′𝑖subscriptsuperscript𝒫′′𝑖𝐸𝙶subscriptsuperscript𝒫′𝑖𝐸𝙶subscriptsuperscript𝒫′𝑖E(\mathtt{G}(\mathcal{P}^{\prime}_{i},\mathcal{P}^{\prime\prime}_{i}))=E(\mathtt{G}(\mathcal{P}^{\prime}_{i}))\cup E(\mathtt{G}(\mathcal{P}^{\prime}_{i})). Thus every edge in 𝙶​(𝒫i′,𝒫i′′)𝙶subscriptsuperscript𝒫′𝑖subscriptsuperscript𝒫′′𝑖\mathtt{G}(\mathcal{P}^{\prime}_{i},\mathcal{P}^{\prime\prime}_{i}) corresponds to a path in Hisubscript𝐻𝑖H_{i}. We can therefore conclude that for a cycle in 𝙶​(𝒫i′,𝒫i′′)𝙶subscriptsuperscript𝒫′𝑖subscriptsuperscript𝒫′′𝑖\mathtt{G}(\mathcal{P}^{\prime}_{i},\mathcal{P}^{\prime\prime}_{i}), there exists a corresponding cycle in Hisubscript𝐻𝑖H_{i}, which contradicts the fact that Hisubscript𝐻𝑖H_{i} is acyclic. Hence 𝙶​(𝒫i′,𝒫i′′)𝙶subscriptsuperscript𝒫′𝑖subscriptsuperscript𝒫′′𝑖\mathtt{G}(\mathcal{P}^{\prime}_{i},\mathcal{P}^{\prime\prime}_{i}) is acyclic.∎

Finally, consider i,j∈[n]𝑖𝑗delimited-[]𝑛i,j\in[n]. Recall that V​(Gt′)∩V​(Gt′′)=Xt𝑉subscript𝐺superscript𝑡′𝑉subscript𝐺superscript𝑡′′subscript𝑋𝑡V(G_{t^{\prime}})\cap V(G_{t^{\prime\prime}})=X_{t} and π​(j)∩Xt=Sj𝜋𝑗subscript𝑋𝑡subscript𝑆𝑗\pi(j)\cap X_{t}=S_{j}. Hence vi​(π​(j))=vi​(π​(j)∩V​(Gt′))+vi​(π​(j)∩V​(Gt′′))−vi​(π​(j)∩Xt)=wi​j′+wi​j′′−vi​(Sj)subscript𝑣𝑖𝜋𝑗subscript𝑣𝑖𝜋𝑗𝑉subscript𝐺superscript𝑡′subscript𝑣𝑖𝜋𝑗𝑉subscript𝐺superscript𝑡′′subscript𝑣𝑖𝜋𝑗subscript𝑋𝑡subscriptsuperscript𝑤′𝑖𝑗subscriptsuperscript𝑤′′𝑖𝑗subscript𝑣𝑖subscript𝑆𝑗v_{i}(\pi(j))=v_{i}(\pi(j)\cap V(G_{t^{\prime}}))+v_{i}(\pi(j)\cap V(G_{t^{\prime\prime}}))-v_{i}(\pi(j)\cap X_{t})=w^{\prime}_{ij}+w^{\prime\prime}_{ij}-v_{i}(S_{j}). This fact, along with Claim 6.10 and the definitions of η′superscript𝜂′\eta^{\prime} and η′′superscript𝜂′′\eta^{\prime\prime}, shows that η𝜂\eta is (η′,η′′)superscript𝜂′superscript𝜂′′(\eta^{\prime},\eta^{\prime\prime})-consistent. That is, (η′,η′′)∈𝒞(t′,t′′)​(η)superscript𝜂′superscript𝜂′′subscript𝒞superscript𝑡′superscript𝑡′′𝜂(\eta^{\prime},\eta^{\prime\prime})\in\mathcal{C}_{(t^{\prime},t^{\prime\prime})}(\eta).

Therefore, there exist vertices z,z′,z′′∈V​(C)𝑧superscript𝑧′superscript𝑧′′𝑉𝐶z,z^{\prime},z^{\prime\prime}\in V(C) such that z​z′∈E​(C)∩E​(Fi′)𝑧superscript𝑧′𝐸𝐶𝐸subscriptsuperscript𝐹′𝑖zz^{\prime}\in E(C)\cap E(F^{\prime}_{i}) and z​z′′∈E​(C)∩E​(Fi′′)𝑧superscript𝑧′′𝐸𝐶𝐸subscriptsuperscript𝐹′′𝑖zz^{\prime\prime}\in E(C)\cap E(F^{\prime\prime}_{i}); we call such a vertex z𝑧z a flip vertex. We have thus shown that Fisubscript𝐹𝑖F_{i} is indeed a spanning forest for Gt​[π​(i)]subscript𝐺𝑡delimited-[]𝜋𝑖G_{t}[\pi(i)]. Fix i∈[n]𝑖delimited-[]𝑛i\in[n]. Let z,z′∈Si𝑧superscript𝑧′subscript𝑆𝑖z,z^{\prime}\in S_{i}. Fix i∈[n]𝑖delimited-[]𝑛i\in[n] and z∈ϕ​(i)∖Xt𝑧italic-ϕ𝑖subscript𝑋𝑡z\in\phi(i)\setminus X_{t}. Claims 6.11-6.14 show that Fisubscript𝐹𝑖F_{i} is indeed a (t,η,i)𝑡𝜂𝑖(t,\eta,i)-witness for ϕitalic-ϕ\phi. We can thus conclude that ϕitalic-ϕ\phi is a (t,η)𝑡𝜂(t,\eta)-valid allocation and hence A​[t,η]=1𝐴𝑡𝜂1A[t,\eta]=1. And 6 correctly assigns the value 111 to A​[t,η]𝐴𝑡𝜂A[t,\eta].

∎

We proposed an alternative for connectivity in the fair division of graphs. Our results demonstrate that we can achieve tractability results under such alternative constraints. Our results also demonstrate that a number of tools and deep results from graph theory could find applications in fair division; this is still an under-explored direction. Compact allocations, we believe, can be a compelling alternative for connected allocations, and warrant further study. As we noted in Section 1, compactness generalises the connectivity constraint as well.

This work leaves several questions open. First, it would be interesting to see if our algorithmic results translate to the strongly compact setting. Second, all our strong NP-hardness results rely on a arbitrary number of agents and non-identical valuations. It would be interesting to see if more restricted hardness results can be proved.

Apart from connectivity and compactness, there may be other structured bundles that are worth investigating. In situations where the graph models a spatial relationship among the items—rooms in a building, for example—connectivity or compactness may be the most appropriate choices for the bundles. But as we noted in Section 1, graphs can model a variety of relationships among the items. It is pertinent to consider what other graph theoretic restrictions on the bundles would be useful when the graph models non-spatial relationships among the items, say similarity of the items based on rather abstract features.We hope this work will trigger such questions.
